B008AS5UAO|5.0|Given the number of recordings available of Mozart's great masterpiece, including at least a few that come close to complete perfection, could yet another recording of Don Giovanni possibly have anything new to offer?<br /><br />That question is answered with a resounding yes only a few bars into Maestro N&eacute;zet-S&eacute;guin's dynamic, effusive rendition of the overture. N&eacute;zet-S&eacute;guin rips through the overture, and indeed most of the opera, at breakneck speed, and with absolutely dazzling results. The drama is accelerated and intensified, not only through truly remarkable and ingeniously executed tempi, but also through masterful control of the orchestra's dynamics. The textures that the maestro carefully coaxes from the Mahler Chamber Orchestra can only be described as glorious. However, with a truly extraordinary cast of world class singers, N&eacute;zet-S&eacute;guin's conducting is hardly the only compelling reason to own this recording.<br /><br />Amid an ensemble of world-class talent, it is the two female leads, Diana Damrau (as Donna Anna) and Joyce DiDonato (as Donna Elvira), who offer the most electrifying performances, both musically and dramatically. DiDonato's Elvira is particularly unhinged, in a truly frightening and very sad characterization that fastidiously avoids the silly, hackneyed histrionics employed so often by lesser singers in this role. DiDonato's artistic creativity seems completely unrestrained in the role, yet her characterization nevertheless remains completely faithful to Da Ponte's and Mozart's depiction of their tragic \\"donna abbandonata\\". From a technical perspective, DiDonato's performance can only be described as being virtually flawless.<br /><br />As Donna Anna, Diana Damrau brings real life and a depth of characterization to the role that is rarely seen today. Instead of the static figure so often portrayed, we get a sense of Donna Anna's humanity and her truly human desire for retribution for her father's killer. Damrau's execution of the role is technically brilliant, unquestionable affirming her credential as a master Mozartian.<br /><br />Ildebrando D'Arcangelo offers a vocally strong Don Giovanni with a deeply resonant lyric bass. While D'Arcangelo's choice to portray Don Giovanni as rather anonymous character and man of mystery perhaps comes across as being somewhat flat and unnuanced, this intentional artistic choice on D'Arcangelo's part is exactly how Da Ponte and Mozart present their anti-hero; we see nothing of Don Giovanni's inner life, and all we learn about Don Giovanni comes from his interactions with the other characters. While this dramatic approach is far more likely to succeed on stage than on an audio-only recording, D'Arcangelo's pure lyricism more than makes up for any perceived lack of dramatic flair. The unique timbre of D'Arcangelo's instrument makes it easy to distinguish between the two bass-baritone roles in the opera, Don Giovanni and his manservant, Leporello, who is sung with impeccable comic timing and skillful musicianship by Luca Pisaroni.<br /><br />Tenor Rolando Villaz&oacute;n, making his return to opera, in mostly good form, after a multiennial hiatus from performing following surgery to remove a cyst from his vocal chords, offers a rather perplexing take on the role of Don Ottavio. While Villaz&oacute;n puts in an overall solid vocal performance, his tone is a bit rough for such a lyrical role, and his legato, at times, simply doesn't seem to be there. Perhaps hoping to compensate with added dramatic oomph, Villaz&oacute;n offers up a more fiery and assertive take on Don Ottavio. This seems to be a rather confused interpretation given that throughout the opera Ottavio is passivity and impotence personified. He spends the entire opera groveling to his beloved Donna Anna and instead of doing anything himself to find her attacker. This simply dosen't fit with Villaz&oacute;n's interpretation.  While Villaz&oacute;n's presence was likely a boost for marketing and publicity purposes for Deutsche Grammophon, the recording would have been better off with any number of lesser known but more capable tenors in the role.<br /><br />I should note that this recording employs a fortepiano, rather than a harpsichord, as the keyboard instrument for the continuo. This would be less of a problem if the use of the fortepiano were limited to the recitatives. However, Benjamin Bayl's fortepiano improvisations are heard in the orchestral ritornellos throughout the opera, and to rather disconcerting effect. The next recording in this series, Cos&igrave; fan tutte, is scheduled for release in August 2013. Let us hope that Maestro N&eacute;zet-S&eacute;guin has the wisdom and good taste to do away with the fortepiano and the improvisations for that release, as they unfortunately mar an otherwise flawless orchestral rendition on this recording.<br /><br />The recording, which was made in a live concert performance of the opera, is of outstanding quality and is completely unmarred by audience noise or any other extraneous sounds. The recording is extremely well mastered, allowing both the vocal performances and N&eacute;zet-S&eacute;guin's brilliant conducting to be richly reproduced in vibrant stereo sound. In terms of audio quality, it is the highest quality recording of Don Giovanni currently available. Highly recommended.

B00005YUBL|5.0|This set of recordings from 1972 has been in my collection for forty years now and this latest set of remastered discs is certainly worth acquiring as the recordings have never sounded better and originally sounded far from clear, even if always thrilling. The original sound was too generous in its acoustics and produced somewhat 'swimmy sounds' where detail got submerged in the venue. This has now been completely rectified and is no longer a problem.<br /><br />The performances themselves have a remarkable sweep and exhilaration apparent from first note to last. This may have something to do with the circumstances of their making. The orchestra and conductor were originally booked to record Wagner's Rienzi but at the last moment two singers pulled out and that recording had to be abandoned. It was decided to use the booked time slot to make a recording of this set of Schumann. The orchestra was already very familiar with Schumann's work with a history of that link going back to the time when Schumann lived in Dresden. The change of direction for the recording sessions must have introduced an element of freshness and spontaneity with little opportunity to over-rehearse. The result, as one American reviewer put it, was 'Sawallisch's white-hot direction nails you to the wall.'<br /><br />This is one of those sets where absolutely everything seems to be perfect. Schumann's symphonies have an inner glow and compulsion in these performances that leaves most of the competition far behind. others may, and certainly do, bring other values to these works but for sheer excitement, verve, spontaneity and incandescence, these discs are in a class of their own.<br /><br />I would suggest that, no matter now many other recordings collectors have of these works, this set appropriately listed as one of the Great Recordings of the Century, is a 'must have' set. For those who are yet to buy their first or only copy of these works, this set has to be considered as one of the very best to put on the short-list.to put on the short-list.

0195145925|4.0|Is time a mere illusion? British theoretical physicist Julian Barbour argues that time itself does not exist in the universe. He claims that both time and motion is an illusion our brain creates for our human-centric perception of a physically static universe. Barbour's claim is certainly provocative. I do not wish to quarrel with him regarding his claim's technical soundness. Having read his book, The End of Time, I managed to remain respectful of his main proposition and ingenuity.<br /><br />Philosophers often point out to theoretical physicists who are marching into their traditional territory that they are in fact dealing with the traditional problems of philosophy that won't be solved using scientific methodology, which is basically hypothetical inductive reasoning. Stephen Hawking is one prominent theoretical physicist who rejects philosophers' such criticism - with no good either scientific or philosophical counter-argument - and even declared almost out of scientific fanaticism, \\"Philosophy is dead.\\" I personally wish that I could bet on Hawking's religious faith in what he loosely deems as \\"science.\\" But I have to agree with his critics that theoretical scientists like Hawking or Barbour for that matter are in fact no longer doing science since their claims are purely based on mathematical crunching and therefore not possible either to confirm or refute based on observation/experiments, a core scientific methodology.<br /><br />I also see Barbour running into the problem of paradox that Thomas Kuhn's critics raised for his The Structure of Scientific Revolutions. If Barbour is right (time is indeed an illusion), we would have very little reason to believe in his own claim since he would have ironically ended up destroying the very foundation of science - built on a priori existence of time and space - which many other established theories he borrowed were also built upon. If Barbour is indeed right, we no longer have any reason to believe in science's, and also Barbour's, presumption that the whole world we observe is physical, out there independently, and also governed by the law of causation which has nothing to do with our subjective consciousness. I am not sure if he can escape from this paradoxical self-contradiction which ultimately destroyed credibility of Kuhn's otherwise brilliant intellectual accomplishment. It is somewhat eerie to recall a Buddhist philosopher's argument that all (Western) scientific statements are bound to prove self-contradictory in the end (because of its \\"religious\\" metaphysical presumption that there is a physical world independently out there - e.g., traditional monotheism based on the presumption of existence of the creator God won't make much sense if there is no independent physical world \\"out there.\\"<br /><br />Barbour spent most of his book's pages to show - with some ingenuity - how the universe as a theoretical construct of the modern physics can be also re-interpreted to be completely static (in a sense, this type of argument is clever rearranging of the existing theories). He focuses on removing time from an equation of physics since time poses a deeply troubling problem for modern physics. He then simply and quite conveniently tosses over to neuroscientists the heavier task of explaining how the human brain (or consciousness) produces a consistent, extremely well-regulated and relentless movie out of a timeless and motionless universe. No offense intended, but I've found his shockingly naive understanding of neuroscience here almost unbelievable; isn't a human brain also simply part of a physical universe subject to constant changes he denies?<br /><br />I am not sure if Barbour fully realizes that the very foundation of modern physics will shatter and its devastating theoretical consequences - even for his type of theory itself - if time is indeed not real. One may also ask the single most persistent question of philosophy here: which comes first, mind or matter? If time is not `real' after all, we have little reason to believe that we are in fact real (not that I insist that we have to be real, whatever 'real' means). It only bolsters idealists' skepticism that we do not know that there is actually a `real' universe out there then (not that I reject their stance, but it only means modern science then proves to be nothing but a sophisticated but completely wrong human imagination.)<br /><br />Barbour is a rare independent academic doing serious research outside an ivory tower. The mainstream physics community seems to be rather ignoring or reluctant to embrace his clever theorizing out of established laws of physics and theories (no surprise here^^). Barbour's theory - like those of many contemporary theoretical physicists - cannot be either falsified or experimented for confirmation, which raises another question whether this type of speculation growing among contemporary theoretical physicists today is really science. Karl Popper, probably the most influential philosopher of science who's shaped a mainstream modern conception of science, would also deny since there is no way to falsify Barbour's kind of theories via either observation or experiment. Besides whether his idea is a falsifiable-therefore-scientific theory of physics or not, I nonetheless find his underlying idea - personally - alluring in that his conclusion is consistent with what many great philosophers and ancient Buddhists have envisioned of the universe.<br /><br />Time has been a consistently puzzling topic for many philosophers, both ancient and modern. No truly great philosopher ever missed the critical importance of time for our self-conscious existence. Even from a philosophical perspective, I believe that Barbour's hypothesis is worth considering since making time `an illusion' is one logical way to remove a persistent puzzle of time from modern physics, although that will put us right back into the original box of puzzle again (which in my opinion should be rather embraced for new thinking); Newton was well aware of this paradox when he simply decided to accept both time and space as \\"absolute\\" without offering any scientific rationale (and his secretly but deeply religious idea persists even today). The idea that time does not exist is nothing new in the history of philosophy. But the theoretical claim, whether philosophical, spiritual or scientific,  based on speculation alone does not make time go away. For me, many modern physicists' theory of time sounds increasingly boring since it is all purely speculative, whether peppered with mathematical equations or not. In the end, time persists for everyone of us as so real as before.<br /><br />Not only ancient Buddhists but gifted Western philosophers often arrived at the same conclusion that time might be mere illusion - that is, from a logical, analytically, spiritual or even meditative perspective. Why are those non-ordinary perspective telling us truth or more truthful than our everyday experience we all share though? Physicists, even one as gifted as Einstein or Newton, were always puzzled by the phenomena of time but had never seriously denied the very realness of time itself. Barbour as a theoretical physicist is perhaps to be noted in that regard alone.s not `real' after all, we have little reason to believe that we are in fact real (not that I insist that we have to be real, whatever 'real' means). Brando has second billing to Martin Sheen but he does not appear until the last act of the film.  Keep in mind that this movie is over three hours. I like how they built Kurtz up throughout the movie and I like story behind him, but I still wish he was in the film more.<br /><br />This movie has weird passing issues as well.  The majority of this movie feels like padding.  The overall plot revolves around Willard going kill Kurtz, but ninety percent of this movie is him getting to his destination.  I know it was like this in order to showcase some of the Vietnam War.  Some of it works and some of it does not.  I like the scenes showcasing the war.  There isnot that much action though.  The biggest action scene of the whole movie was near the beginning.  This might turn some people off who are expecting big action scenes like in Saving Private Ryan.  However this film does a great job at depicting how the Vietnam War was.  The film also has a bleak atmosphere throughout most of which definitely fit the setting.<br /><br />However, there are some scenes in the film that I have no clue why they are even in the movie.  There is this one long scene near the beginning that focused on this weird General that likes to surf, which is weird especially since we see him ever again.  There is this very drawn out scene in which Willard and his crew stop at this run down barracks and proceed to flirt with all the women there.  The weirdest scene is when the crew meets these French people and have dinner with them.  There is also this mini romance between Willard and this French woman, which felt extremely out of place.  It really felt like I was watching a different film when I saw that.  I do not know if these scenes were in the original or if they were added back in for this version, but I am going with ladder.  All of those scenes felt extremely pointless, and I do not know what they were for.<br /><br />I love the look of the film.  The setting looks very much like Vietnam.  The few action scenes there were I enjoyed.  The score was amazing.  I also like the atmosphere throughout most the film.<br /><br />Overall Apocalypse Now Redux is a good movie and, to be honest, one of my favorite war movies.  However there was not that much action, which might turn some off.  Plus there are many pointless and drawn out scenes which can get very boring.  It is not really a film that can be watched again and again.  However, I highly recommend that you see this film at least once.

0062255657|5.0|Haunting.<br /><br />If I had only one word to describe this book, it would be 'haunting.'<br /><br />In all, it is a hard book to describe, just as experiences and memories are hard to describe even to a person who shared the event that gave rise to the experience and memory.  And this is what the book is about, the personal, idiosyncratic nature of memory and experience.  Or at least this is one of the things the book is about.<br /><br />The tale definitely has the feel of a short story, but a short story that could not accept its boundaries. It is a simple story told simply, revealing a complexity hidden beneath the surface simplicity that enchants and lulls you into its depths.  It is a pond that hides an Ocean.<br /><br />Adults are sure that their lives are more complex than children's.  But is that a surface complexity that belies an underlying narrowing down of possibilities from a child's borderless world?  As Gaiman says, \\"Adults follow paths. Children explore.\\"<br /><br />As adults, is it because our minds have gotten narrower, smaller, less complex that we can't remember so much from our childhood?  Do our mental constrictions that allow us to focus on the pragmatics of our daily life preclude the depth of experience open to any 7-year old?<br /><br />This story drew out of the Ocean depths of my memory experiences from my own childhood that I hadn't thought about in ages.  Part of the haunting character of the tale is this nostalgic provocation. This heartsickness to capture the feel of home and childhood again.  The time when adults were both a source of comfort and a source of terror.  As the boy in the story says, children experience and deal with terrors that an adult would not be able to bear.<br /><br />This book will speak to those who grew up buried in books and in their imaginations.  People who, as children, saw other humans as dangerous and sought sanctuary in books.  Seeking companionship lays you open to harm and the boy in the story discovers this to be true, not just theoretically but factually.  However, he finds that seeking companionship can sometimes also lead to finding a partner willing to share your risks and to combine efforts with you in fighting off the dangers of the world.<br /><br />To the reviewers hesitant to buy because of the brevity of the work: a true reader values a work by the experience given, not by the page count.  In this novel/novella, the brevity is perfect; it allows you to explore the Ocean beneath this seeming pond by diving down into your own experiences and memories.

B0014Z4ON4|3.0|A divisive chapter among fans of the series, Temple of Doom is easily the silliest of the initial Indiana Jones trilogy. While I've heard the argument that this character thrives on fantastical situations and traces of lore, for my money the envelope is pressed just a bit too far in this instance. Sure, Raiders used the power of the ark to melt the Nazis' skin and Crusade showcased an immortal knight with a collection of stand-in grails, but in each case those represented the climax of a long, grounded adventure - a mere taste of supernatural payoff. Temple shows no such restraint, diving straight in with voodoo dolls, mysterious brainwashing liquids and, memorably, bare-handed heart removals. It also tinkers with the formula of Jones as a loner, with mixed success. Indy's de-facto sidekick, Short Round, plays up every stereotype of a kid tagalong. He's shoehorned in, no doubt about it, but also adds a new dimension to the larger-than-life lead character via their rapid-fire rapport. The additional presence of a blonde love interest, Willie, seems redundant and unnecessary - her constant shrieks and clueless nature gives the impression Indy's babysitting two kids. Of course, it's not all bad news: Harrison Ford works wonders with his shadier lines and knocks the good ones right out of the park, the comic relief scenes (though over-applied) work surprisingly well, and the action / adventure elements the series is best known for hit all the right buttons. There's no shortage of that old, familiar formula here, but I wonder if Spielberg and Lucas may have overreached in an effort to make the film more palatable to the Saturday morning cartoon crowd.

B0000634EV|5.0|This album is just perfect, what can I really say? I mean it may not be near as heavy as the classic 1995 debut masterpiece &#34;NOLA&#34; was, but there's no question that &#34;Down II: A Bustle in Your Hedgerow&#34; is an awesome masterpiece in it's own right, and an awesome follow up release to &#34;NOLA&#34; as well. While &#34;NOLA&#34; was more straight up heavy and in your face, this album has a much more 70's heavy metal, hard rock, southern blues vibe to it with a mix of Black Sabbath, Deep Purple, Lynyrd Skynyrd, and Led Zeppelin, and yes even the album's subtitle is a reference borrowed from the lyrics of Zeppelin's epic masterpiece &#34;Stairway to Heaven&#34;. With Pantera bassist Rex Brown (who replaces Todd Strange), and producer Warren Riker, Down moved into singer Philip Anselmo's barn, dubbed &#34;Nodferatu's Lair&#34; located in Southern Louisiana where they lived and recorded the album in 28 days without anyone leaving the house. Philip Anselmo is in excellent form here captivating the listener throughout with his amazing singing abilities on here most of the time rather than his trademark screams and shouts that he was well known for back in his days in Pantera, meanwhile Kirk Windstein and Pepper Keenan both do an awesome job at pounding out riff after riff with pure perfection, and of course Rex Brown's bass really shines on here throughout as does Jimmy Bower's drumming providing a very thick and swampy rhythm section.<br /><br />Highlights on this awesome masterpiece of an album include the monstrous and heavy stomping opener &#34;Lysergik Funeral Procession&#34; (which includes a very memorable Sabbath-esque riff), &#34;There's Something on My Side&#34; (which features a catchy drum and bass intro plus more awesome brewing riffs as well as a cool melodic, swampy breakdown at 2:08 before the heaviness resumes around 3:11), &#34;The Man That Follows Hell&#34;, &#34;Stained Glass Cross&#34; (which has a very catchy southern blues rock vibe especially in the chorus), and there's also my favorite track &#34;Ghosts Along the Mississippi&#34; (which features an awesome opening riff plus excellent singing vocals from Phil and a great solo as well), and &#34;Learn From This Mistake&#34; (which is a nice slow and melodic number that includes some great bluesy melodic lead guitar work), and there's also &#34;Beautifully Depressed&#34;, &#34;Where I'm Going&#34;, &#34;New Orleans is a Dying Whore&#34;, &#34;The Seed&#34;, and the brilliant Zeppelin-esque acoustic closer &#34;Landing on the Mountains of Meggido&#34; which features guest vocals from Phil's ex-wife Stephanie Opal Weinstein. It's such a brilliant way to conclude the album, although it may not be as great as &#34;Bury Me in Smoke&#34; from &#34;NOLA&#34;, but it's still brilliant nonetheless.<br /><br />All in all, &#34;Down II: A Bustle in Your Hedgerow&#34; is an awesome sophomore album from start to finish, and if you enjoyed &#34;NOLA&#34;, then by all means you'll definitely enjoy this album for sure. True, it might not be as heavy as &#34;NOLA&#34;, but it is an awesome follow up nonetheless...Highly Recommended!!!n the chorus), and there's also my favorite track &#34;Ghosts Along the Mississippi&#34; (which features an awesome opening riff plus excellent singing vocals from Phil and a great solo as well), and &#34;Learn From This Mistake&#34; (which is a nice slow and melodic number that includes some great bluesy melodic lead guitar work), and there's also &#34;Beautifully Depressed&#34;, &#34;Where I'm Going&#34;, &#34;New Orleans is a Dying Whore&#34;, &#34;The Seed&#34;, and the brilliant Zeppelin-esque acoustic closer &#34;Landing on the Mountains of Meggido&#34; which features guest vocals from Phil's ex-wife Stephanie Opal Weinstein. 076535618X|4.0|Originally published at FanLit.<br /><br />The Last Colony, the third book in John Scalzi's OLD MAN'S WAR series, returns us to the perspective of John Perry, the \\"old man\\" hero of the first novel in the series, Old Man's War. John Perry is only mentioned in the second novel, The Ghost Brigades, which told the story of how the cyborg Special Forces soldiers found and defeated the scientist Charles Boutin, a traitor to the Colonial Union. On that mission they also found Zoe, Boutin's young daughter. Zoe has been adopted by Jane Sagan and John Perry and the little family has been farming on one of Earth's colonies where John and Jane are the leaders.<br /><br />Life is easy for them until the Colonial Union comes calling -- they need leaders for a new colonization effort and John and Jane have been selected. This new colony (named Roanoke.... hmmmm... I think I wouldn't have signed up for that) will be comprised of people from several different human worlds and John and Jane are responsible for its success. However, the Colonial Union hasn't been completely honest with them. It will be a lot more dangerous than the members of Roanoke have been led to believe. They are being played as political pawns and they don't realize it until it's too late. And it's not just Roanoke that's in danger, but the entire human race.<br /><br />The Last Colony (I keep wanting to write \\"The Lost Colony\\") has a different tone than Old Man's War and The Ghost Brigades. It takes place mainly on a planet, rather than in space, and deals mostly with domestic and political matters rather than space battles and espionage. Some of the political dialogue between characters we don't know is dull, especially if you're hoping for lasers and explosions, but Scalzi continues to explore the interesting theme of access to information and the problems that occur when the government controls the press. When and how should governments control information? That's always a relevant topic, isn't it?<br /><br />Like its predecessors, The Last Colony features John Scalzi's engaging writing style and ultra-competent well-developed characters. Some of these are characters we already know and love (John and Jane) one is a character we are happy we're getting to know (Zoe) and some are new characters that Scalzi makes it easy for us to love (e.g., the Mennonite leader, Hickory and Dickory) or hate (e.g., the journalists). And some are there to show us that our first impressions aren't always correct.<br /><br />I mentioned in my review of The Ghost Brigades that the political situation was getting murky and it gets even murkier here. It is not clear to us (or to many of the characters) whose side we should be on. Readers may find it discomfiting to realize they are having trouble sympathizing with their home planet. It may be even more discomfiting to realize that Scalzi's story doesn't have to stretch the imagination too far. Sometimes \\"human nature\\" is not a pretty thing, but it's what we know. What if someday we find ourselves needing to interact with beings who have a non-human nature?<br /><br />You can probably read The Last Colony without having read the previous books, Old Man's War and The Ghost Brigades, but you'll have some catching up to do. It would be better to wait on this one until you've read its predecessors. They're both great books, anyway. The fourth book in the OLD MAN'S WAR series is Zoe's Tale which tells the story of Roanoke colony from Zoe's perspective. It's mostly the exact same plot as The Last Colony with a few side adventures for Zoe. If you're only interested in the plot progression, you can skip Zoe's Tale. If you're interested in getting to know Zoe, you should read it.<br /><br />I'm listening to William Dufris narrate OLD MAN'S WAR. I think he's amazing. Macmillan Audio produced this installment./>Like its predecessors, The Last Colony features John Scalzi's engaging writing style and ultra-competent well-developed characters. Rock, hip hop, metal, House, pop, indie, ambient, etc.  Sigur Ros has always had a special place in my heart with their music.  I can proudly say that they are my all time favorite band and I will listen to them for the rest of my life no matter what.  Sigur Ros has mostly been categorized as Post Rock, but they are their own genre in my opinion.  They have always made some of the most beautiful music I have ever heard.  To me, good music is good music regardless of whether it is mainstream popular or underground.  Sigur Ros make great and dreamy music that channels all kinds of emotions. My favorite albums of course were their untitled album \\"( )\\",\\"Takk\\" and of course \\"Agaetis Byrjun\\". I first discovered the band through their musical appearance in the movie \\"Vanilla Sky\\" and I was hooked. Since then I listened to all of their albums.  Then I heard of their new album \\"Kveikur\\" being a new and more aggressive sound. I was curious and looked up their first two singles \\"Brennisteinn\\" and \\"Isjaki\\". The former had a very industrial heavy sound and reminded me of Silversun Pickups a bit. I liked the feeling it gave me. It was almost an apocalyptic feeling. Then I heard \\"Isjaki\\", and I was blown away by the beauty of it. It was very upbeat and poppy, but still had the heavenly unique Sigur Ros vibe. I was sold, I wanted this album. I also heard that Sigur Ros signed with the record label \\"XL\\" which mostly features indie music. The most well known of the label are \\"Vampire Weekend\\", \\"Adele\\", and \\"Radiohead\\", so I was anxious to hear how signing to \\"XL\\" would change the music. There have been hints that this album will be the most commercial sounding as well. Like I said, I listen to all kinds of music and this new album was released on the same day as many other albums I was anticipating including Kanye Wests new controversial \\"Yeezus\\". I was standing in Best Buy for 30 minutes contemplating what to buy. Finally Idecided on \\"Kviekur\\", and I am betting I was the only one that day to bring that album to the register. But I didn't care, I just wanted to hear the beauty of this album. So I listened to it three times before I decided to review it and hear is a track by track overview!<br /><br />1. Brennisteinn: This is by far the heaviest song on the album, and it still has very divine vocals. The songs deep bass gives it an \\"End of the World\\" feel. Near the halfway mark of this nearly 8 minute epic, the song changes and becomes faster in the vain of songs from the band Silversun Pickups! Very beautifully haunting. The last minute and a half is a very relaxing recovery from the beautifully musical aggressiveness that just happened in the song. If Brennisteinn was the War, this song is the footage of the aftermath. I mean that in the best way. The vocals from Jon are as beautiful and soaring as always!<br />3. Isjaki: Definitely the most radio ready song. Very upbeat and gorgeous. The vocals kind of remind me of the band \\"Beach House\\". This song brings about so many emotions. It is simply perfection in music form. This is the type of song that would play while you make love in a dream. This song will make you wanna dance and for some reason it makes me feel nostalgic. While listening to this song think of that special someone, or \\"the one who got away\\" and see how you feel! My definite favorite of the album.<br />4. YfirborÃ°: The song starts off slow and peaceful, with another haunting vocal effect in the background. While Jon sings gracefully along with the beautiful music the tempo becomes faster, but doesn't turn into a dance song. It somehow manages to speed up during the chorus without fully becoming an upbeat song. It's so relaxing. The song makes me feel like I am soaring through the clouds and looking at the landscape below!<br />5. Stormur: The song begins slowly with powerful vocals that slightly remind me of the Enigma song \\"Return to Innocence\\". The song then gains momentum and the tempo really picks up. Much like the song \\"Isjaki\\" this song could be released to US radio even though its not in English. I love it. Such a powerful song.  This song can be compared to the song \\"Saeglopur\\" from the bands album \\"Takk\\".  The chiming sound in this song is so infectious.  Definitely one of Sigur Ros's best!<br />6. Kveikur: The title track with a industrial influence like \\"Brennisteinn\\". The song has a big stadium feeling to it. Rafstraumur: After the slight heaviness of \\"Kveikur\\", this song takes you down a notch to just sit back and groove along. The upbeat nature of this song reminds me of Silversun Pickups again. B00CV5ZPA2|5.0|I have always loved Kanye Wests music.  I never really liked his personality in public, but I love his music.  All of his albums are Hip Hop classics.  His first three releases were all Grammy nominated for Album of the Year.  \\"Graduation\\" changed Hip Hop forever with its stadium influenced sound.  Then again, he changed how rap can sound with his album \\"808s and Heartbreaks\\" by adding autotune and giving the genre a more experimental and emotional sound.  The album paved the way for artists such as Kid Cudi and Drake.  Then in 2010 he released what can arguably be labeled his ultimate masterpiece, \\"My Beautiful Dark Twisted Fantasy\\".  It was an epic experimental album that paid tribute to all of the genres Kanye explored through his career with many additional new sounds.  The album was expected to WIN album of the year at the Grammys, but was ultimately snubbed of even a nomination.  Most people, including West himself, blame the fact that he released another hip hop classic soon after with Jay Z, the greatest Hip Hop collaboration album of all time \\"Watch the Throne\\".  So 3 years pass since his last solo release and many were wondering how he would top his masterpiece \\"MBDTF\\".  He started speaking about how he didn't want \\"radio\\" songs on his new album and how there would be no singles.  At first I didn't really think it would be a great album when I saw the bad quality videos on YouTube of his song \\"New Slaves\\".  The song was good, but I didn't really get excited for the new album just from that song.  The live videos of the song \\"Black Skinhead\\" didn't help either.  I am not one to get offended by Kanyes lyrics, I just personally thought the song was unappealing.  People started hating on Kanye for these two new songs and I was starting to think the new album would be horrible.  I did feel a bit of hope when I found out that Daft Punk were producing a few tracks, and that the always amazing Justin Vernon of Bon Iver would help out.  Well it was finally releasedand I must say, though it doesn't top his last album, it does stand out among his collection of classics.  Many think it is another masterpiece, and maybe it is, but the truth is, it was just over hyped.  The album is very, bipolar, in a good way.  Here is a quick track by track overview.<br /><br />1.  On Sight:  This song is okay.  It has a good robotic vibe.  The lyrics are okay for Kanyes standards.  A minute into the song there is a slight interlude that has some nice soul. The beat is amazing, and very similar to Marilyn Mansons song \\"Beautiful People\\". I can sorta see this released as a single based on its pumping nature, but I still don't see it as a great song.  Still better than the horrible live version that was on YouTube though.  Another Daft Punk produced song surprisingly.  I expected more.  This one is a grower.  8/10<br />3.  I am a God:  I know many people will hate the song just because of the title.  This is something Kanye is good at, making people mad!  I kinda like the vibe of the song, but it also gets tiresome quickly.  Most people don't realize he isn't claiming to be GOD, he is saying he is A God.  He is a god of hip hop, you cant deny that.  Despite the egotistical lyrics, this is a great song to work out to.  The pumping house beat is addicting.  Daft Punk produced this track too, and I'm not surprised.  This is radio potential if they cut out the annoying ending that contains screams and heavy breathing.  9/10<br />4.  New Slaves:  Good song, but honestly, I skip over it.  The album versionis refreshing after the annoying live version that was released prior.  Again, for people who get offended by the title, the song isn't a racist song at all.  Frank Ocean makes an appearance at the end, but it doesn't save the song for me.  The song has a similar feel to the songs on Kanyes GOOD music album \\"Cruel Summer\\", mostly the song \\"Clique\\".  8/10<br />5.  Hold My Liquor:  Just when I was beginning to feel a bit disappointed with the album, this song came next.  I think this is the best song on the album.  It has a very new and chill sound.  Chief Keef surprisingly sings the chorus in a catchy way.  I never really liked Chief Keef but he did well on this song.  First the Chief Keef chorus starts and it just sounds okay.  The verses by Kanye are amazing and heartfelt with a screeching industrial guitar in the background with a very relaxing beat.  Then the chorus with Chief Keef kicks in, but this time with amazing guitar work who I assume is from Justin Vernon from Bon Iver, who also does amazing vocal work throughout the song.  There is a tasty guitar solo in there too that fits so well into this relaxing song.  You haven't heard a hip hop song like this.  Only from Yeezus.  This can be released as a single.  This song saved the album for me.  10/10<br />6.  I'm In It:  A great song to follow the previous masterpiece of a song.  The beat is very industrial and abstract.  The lyrics are typical Kanye bragging, but it's amazing.  Before Kanyes verse a Jamaican rapper steals the show with his nice speed.  Then surprisingly Justin Vernon of Bon Iver makes another perfect vocal appearance!  Futuristic hip hop song.  9.5/10<br />7.  Blood on The Leaves:  Great soulful song.  Kanye uses slight autotune and it works so well.  I'm not a fan of Autotune, but Kanye is one of the few who make it work so well.  The sample is similar to Kanyes older song \\"I Wonder\\" from the \\"Graduation\\" album.  Another song that saves the album!  The beat is so hype and perfect!  I don'tknow what else to say.  I love it.  10/10<br />8.  Guilt Trip:  Another great song.  I thought Daft Punk produced it, because it has the most Daft Punk feeling vibe, but sadly they didn't.  Still a great infectious song. Send It Up:  Another Daft Punk produced song, and you can tell.  The chorus is catchy but this is just an okay song among the recent great songs.  I can see this played in the club though.  8/10<br />10.  Bound 2:  The final song kicks off perfectly.  Arguably the most soulful song.  It contains Kanyes iconic sampling of a classic song.  Reminds me of the song \\"Devil in a New Dress\\" from \\"MBDTF\\", and surprisingly this one is better.  Singer Charlie Wilson makes a vocal appearance and he sounds great with the song.  The song has a very romantic hip hop sound, but the lyrics get pretty explicit. Still a perfect album closer that left me wanting so much more!  10/10<br /><br />*First Impressions*<br />So Mr. West has made another classic album.  The only reason the album isn't 5 stars is because the first 4 tracks just weren't up to par with the masterpiece quality of the rest of the album.  Many will love those tracks to death, but I got tired of them quickly.  The album as a whole has this industrial rock influenced sound sometimes similar to early \\"Nine Inch Nails\\" music, but with more Hip Hop elements incorporated.  I recommend the songs \\"Hold My Liquor\\" and \\"Bound 2\\" the most.  Though I would say the last 6 tracks are all the true Highlights and they have the most replay value.  This album will get polarized reviews.  Many are calling it another masterpiece, and many are calling it trash.  It all depends on taste.  But you can't deny that this album is another landmark hip hop album that will surely change the way the genre sounds the way Kanyes other releases have.  I have a feeling Kanye might getanother nomination for Album of The Year after being snubbed with his last true masterpiece.  So if you like good Hip Hop and aren't offended easily then this album is perfect.  This can appeal to anyone who likes good experimental music.  Many have also compared it's experimental genre bending nature to the band Radioheads landmark album \\"Kid A\\", which is actually a compliment!  I also think that like \\"Kid A\\", this album will be hailed as a classic in years to come.  Another good release from the Hip Hop genre this week was J.Coles more commercial sounding \\"Born Sinner\\", but it doesn't stand out like Yeezus.  If you are looking for beautiful music that isn't in the hip hop category then pick up Sigur Ros's 2013 release \\"Kveikur\\".  This album is for music listeners with minds more open to new and different sounds.  Listen to it twice before you form an opinion though!<br /><br />*New thoughts after more repeated listens*<br />I have grown slightly more fond of the first 4 tracks now.  \\"Black Skinhead\\" in particular has become a hit for me.  I still don't see it as a favorite of mine, and it is still not up to par with the last 6 tracks.  But I have heard it in a trailer for the movie \\"The Wolf of Wall Street\\" and I found myself feeling pumped and rapping along.  For some reason \\"Black Skinheads\\" has become very appealing to me and apparently the country.  It is starting to have the same appeal as Kanyes single \\"Power\\" which has become a popular choice for commercials and movie trailers.  It is even being released as the first single surprisingly.  As for the rest of the album, I still love the last 6 tracks the most.  I keep discovering new layers to each song with repeated listens.  I will try to revisit the album every now and again since the music is amazing, but too exhausting for constant repeated listening.<br /><br />**Months Later**<br />I decided to give this another listen again.  Suddenly I am listening closer to the lyrics of all the songs.  The first 4tracks too.  \\"I am a God\\" is suddenly one of my favorite controversial songs ever.  The album sounds new and refreshing and nostalgic for some reason.  I am changing my score to a perfect 5 out of 5 now.  This is a real album.  This will be considered a classic milestone for Hip Hop in years to come.  Truly Kanyes \\"Kid A\\".<br /><br />**After Bound 2 success**<br />The album didn't have any mega hits like previous albums.  Black Skinhead has been used in commercials and trailers but hasn't charted well.  But after Kim Kardashian starred in the controversial music video of the song \\"Bound 2\\", things changed.  The song has gotten really popular and is sure to be the big hit of the album.  It is also reigniting interest in the album as it made me come back and listen again.  Once again I'm discovering new elements to the album.  Masterpiece!

1781162646|5.0|Stephen King, who needs no introduction, returns with a short novel in Joyland, published by Titan books as part of the Hard Case Crime series. But even though the book is under three hundred pages, King easily tells a full and fascinating story that fans and non-King readers will easily enjoy.<br /><br />Devin Jones is spending the summer at Joyland, an amusement park on the sunny coast of South Carolina. Jones isn't doing so well; not sure whether he wants to stay in college, plus it's the early seventies and everything seems uncertain. And the other thing is the love of his live has just broken his heart and he kind of wants his world to end.<br /><br />But then he starts working at Joyland, where they don't just sell cotton candy and prizes and rides, but most importantly, they sell fun! He begins to learn the carny life, the carny talk, and the general running of the amusement park, doing a great job as well as being the best guy at \\"wearing the fur.\\" Joyland has its mighty Ferris wheel, reaching to the stars, the various carnies who have been working there for years and have their own interesting eccentricities, and the Horror House.<br /><br />Every amusement park needs its one horror ride, and Horror House is it for Joyland, and this is the ride that has the dark story about it, because some years ago a girl was murdered on the ride, her throat slashed by her supposed boyfriend, her body dumped to the side of the track. She wasn't found until the early hours of the morning by the cleanup crew; her murderer has never been found. It is said that Horror House is now haunted and sometimes when you're on the ride, you might see the ghost of her body floating beside you in the car, that red slit throat looking like a wide smile.<br /><br />Joyland shows how much of a better writer Stephen King has become over the last decade or so, as you have a thrilling horror tale at the heart of the story, but you also have a wonderful character in the teenager, Devin Jones, who has his whole life ahead of him, but feels it is over with his broken heart. Perhaps King was pulling on his own past experience to give this story life and reality that will move the reader, making Joyland stick with them long after they've finished the book.<br /><br />Originally written on June 12, 2013 Â©Alex C. Telander.<br /><br />For more reviews, check out the BookBanter site: http://www.bookbanter.net.

0316228532|2.0|After the unfathomable success of the Harry Potter series, with over 450 million copies sold worldwide, likely making it one of the biggest phenomena of our lifetimes, J. K. Rowling is now back with her first new book in five years.  She now turns to a much more adult story about a quaint little English town where everything is most certainly not as it seems.<br /><br />In the idyllic west country town of Pagford, where things pass at their own pace and everything stays pretty much the same, a change is about to happen.  A respected citizen of the community, Barry Fairbrother suffers a sudden brain aneurysm and dies unexpectedly.  It is a very sad time for the family and for the community, as he touched many lives during his time, as well as being an important member of the town's council.  But Barry's passing is also the lighting of a spark that sets off an explosive chain reaction, as the empty space on the town council starts many wondering who should fill his seat, and a number of unlikely candidates come out of the woodwork.<br /><br />The Casual Vacancy is also the story about a number of the characters of this community, and how they begin to act and react when this person who had an effect on their lives is gone and is no longer there to provide aid and advice.  The book is by no means a happy novel, as these characters make terrible decisions that lead them down a downward spiral of despair.  By the end of the book, the reader is left hoping their might be some sort of cathartic uplift, but Rowling is going for a harsh true-to-life approach here, where things don't all of a sudden get magically better.<br /><br />Overall the book comes off as a letdown, slow and dragging at points, with nothing to drive the reader along to keep reading, as things get worse and worse for just about everyone it seems.  Rowling is perhaps pulling from some earlier experiences in her life before her fame and riches, as there are characters dealing with drug addiction, poverty,marital problems, and a whole host of unsavory issues.  The book also comes off somewhat amateurish, as Rowling constantly references many places throughout this imaginary town that confuse the reader, and could have easily been aided with a handy map at the beginning of the book.  Then there is the large host of characters, featuring many couples of about the same age, some even with the same first letters of their names, which often makes things confusing, and could've been helped with a simple cast list.  Finally, there is the constantly switching P.O.V. from paragraph to paragraph, without any break in between, so that the reader becomes quite untethered and lost at times.<br /><br />The Casual Vacancy was an experiment by Rowling in seeing what happens to a town when an important member dies and all the people he'd had an effect on begin making bad decisions that then effect the rest of the town.  By the end of the book the reader is sad over the events of the book, though Rowling makes it clear that if any of the characters had made the decision to not think of themselves for a moment and to notice that nearby person suffering and help them, things would have come out quite differently.  But because this social message is buried in the clunky format and pitfalls of the book with no satisfactory resolution, the reader is left wondering what was the point of reading this book to the last page.<br /><br />Originally written on January 8, 2013 Â©Alex C. Telander.<br /><br />For more reviews, check out the BookBanter site: http://www.bookbanter.net.

B00BNWWVFG|4.0|This review contains no specific descriptions of plot events. I saw this in the theater so my review will not include an analysis of the Bluray/DVD technical aspects- the picture quality or sound quality. This review is only an \\"IMO\\" review of the theatrical film itself. Coming from Soderbergh, who's stuff is usually different from most mainstream cinema, \\"Side effects\\" was about what I expected, but more twisted. There's always something in his films that pique my interest. \\"Side effects\\" drew me in and then had me going from being into it to not being into it at various points. I found the film was engaging in spite of some inconsistencies. I also liked Rooney Mara in this, very good performance. Coming from Soderbergh, the use of digital photography, amber hues, and an image that sometimes looks a little pasty on screen was no surprise either.<br />As \\"Side effects\\" moves along, the plot goes a bit haywire. I still think it's a movie that is well worthwhile, but it feels more like Soderbergh's political statement on the pharmaceutical industry and Wall Street/insider trading, which is fine by me, but the audience side of the equation could have been better judged. The basic idea itself is not so absurd, but is certainly carried over the top. I don't know, maybe he wants that question to be asked, how sensationalist is this? Severe drug side effects, to include bizarre behavior have been documented, and is anyone going to prove there is no unethical money made on what Wall street, the government, doctor's, and drug companies do lol. Maybe there's a deeper irony at work here. The films main weakness is the plot trips up in technical details- which Soderbergh usually pays more attention to. The plot discrepancies reduce the impact of the film as it morphs between its pharmaceutical side effect theme and its insider trading theme. It sometimes comes across as farcical- but it is no more absurd than what we see in the real world- The railroading of drugs onto the market, enthusiastic dispensal by doctors, the astronomical profits of drug companies; and the money wall street, and people on Capitol hill get on insider trading.<br />\\"Side effects\\" is on the extreme side, is deliberately paced (which anyone familiar with a lot of his stuff won't be surprised at) and try's to cover too much ground as it draws to its conclusion. The acceleration of events- from the slow start to the final act might leave some viewers a little confused. I still liked it better than many other recent offerings. As \\"Psychological Thrillers\\" go, this one will keep you entertained and get you thinking. I liked the concept of \\"side effects\\", and it has the crazy ending of a thriller. It was one of those movies that does'nt quite reach its full potential, and ends up being 3 or 4 stars instead of 5. I give it 3.5 stars. I'd Recommend to people who like a cerebral thriller, and to fans of Rooney Mara.<br />Update: I've since gotten the bluray version of this movie- and found both the sound and picture of the bluray transfer to be very good. Versus how I remember the film looking in the theater, things seem faithful to the color palette of Soderbergh, and everything is a little cleaner and clearer, so maybe they used some \\"DNR\\" in producing the bluray, but it is nothing unqualified, and in this case actually improves over what I saw in the theater.

The FLOYD's trademark components...DAVID GILMOUR's stunning, liquid guitar blurbs, WATERS' cynical lyrics and edgy, gruff vocals, and RICHARD WRIGHT's spacey keyboard textures...are the main draws on A FOOT IN THE DOOR, which lacks samples from important albums like MEDDLE and ANIMALS. This one's mainly recommended to listeners who aren't adventurous enough to purchase individual platters from the band's vast, ethereal catalogue.<br /><br />RATING: FOUR FLOYDS

B00CISC2DA|4.0|\\"Tomorrow's Harvest\\" is the sound of robots making music.  That is not to say it is the sound of human beings controlling robots to make music; rather, this is the sound of robot's creating music in the absence of humanity.  On a vacated Earth where humans have either gone extinct or left for a different world, many of their machines and computers have been left behind.  In the face of a human void, these devices, over a period of time, start to create.<br /><br />The music of the robots is not a music based upon their gaining of sentience -- it is a simulacrum of sentience based upon their being designed and programed by the humans.  With only the traces of our spirits in their binary understandings and vacuum sealed anatomies, they run like motors compelled only by their existence as physical matter.  Slowly, like erosion carving a canyon, they build up something resembling music yet still very much machine.  Via if/then probabilities and their banks of human data (knowledge) a pseudo-music emerges.  The robots \\"understand\\" only those things that are tangible - rhythm, melody, pitch, tone, placement.  Beauty created is but a coincidence because they possess no true understanding of beauty.  But it is beautiful nonetheless.<br /><br />The striving to create music, i.e., beauty, comes about on this cold and dead earth that humans have left behind out of necessity.  When the masters leave this burnt out husk of a planet there will still be a yearning for those wonderful interpretations of existence of which only human beings are capable.<br /><br />In the past BOC have made a music of electronics creating \\"pure\\" and almost \\"natural\\" sounds without resorting to flat-out imitation.  It was as if a synthesizer was displaying the sound of a blue sky.  Today, on \\"Tomorrow's Harvest\\", the listener hears not a musical interpretation of the natural elements but a reclamation of music in a place where music is no longer heard.

0545586178|3.0|I read the Hunger Games so that I could talk about it with my son and watch the movie with him. I am also an author, so I try to read the really popular books to see what people are reading. The premise for the book seemed okay. It's not the first dystopian society book ever written, but it has a huge following so figured it had to be good. It was good, part of it anyway. Katniss has the potential to be a great female character, the premise of the book, fighting each other so as to not starve to death, oppression, the gap between the haves and the have-nots, all good stuff. I just wish the author had been a little bit bolder, a little bit edgier.  It's a story where a small segment of the polulation treats the rest of the world as sub-humans, starving them into submission and using them for their own warped pleasure. Kids murder each other. The author needs to commit all the way, to the horrific violence, not shy away and try to keep it PG just for sales. Some of the parts that confused me were, why does Katniss feel bad that Rue is killed, yet nothing for the boy she kills with the arrow?  Rue, despite their alliance would have eventually tried to kill her. Why can't doesn't she put flowers on the boy who killed Rue, too?<br />I was bitterly disappointed that Katniss did not fight off Clove herself, but is instead rescued by Thresh. Boo! Why would Thresh give her a pass, knowing he'll have to kill her eventually anyway? That was a glaring weakness in the story. Aaaarg! I really wish I could re-write that part of the book.<br />The part that I really hated was the weird Muttation creatures. First, let's backtrack.  The Capitol has all this advanced technology, hover crafts, medicine that cures practically overnight, can build the arenas to control the temperature, the water, etc, yet they rely on coal for fuel from the mines in the Seam? Huh? I would think they would be advanced enough to develop solar and wind power and not be using fossil fuels anymore. They have an orchard district (Rue and Thresh are from there)? Wouldn't they be growing everything they need in hydroponic towers right in the Capitol? So how are we to believe that they are so advanced that they can inject human DNA and intelligence in huge wolf-like creatures? They can make them overnight? That was sooooo far fetched that I was dying to re-write that part.  Why not just set real wolves on them and in a fight on top of the Cornacopia Cato falls and is eaten alive. B004SVM7BW|3.0|I was looking for a PDF annotator for Android that is as good as Goodreader for iPad, because I want to take advantage of an active digital pen in something like the Note 10.1.  This program seems quite good, but is lacking an important feature for navigating easily within a long document.  For working with PDF files that have different pagination sections -- e.g., i, ii, ...{n} for an introductory section, and 1 - 1000 for the main section -- Acrobat (and others) allow the user to assign page numbers within the PDF document that correspond to the published pagination.  Goodreader recognizes the assignment of these page numbers, so that if I want to go to p. ix in the introduction, I can simply by typing \\"ix\\" in the navigation box; or if I want to go to p. 556 in the main part of the document, I can type \\"556.\\"  This program seems not to recognize these pagination designations made in Acrobat, and treats p. i as p. 1, etc.  If I want to go to p. 556 in the text, I have to add the number of pages i ...{n} in the introductory section, and type that number in the navigation pane.  I hope this feature, one that Goodreader has, can be added to this app soon.

B008JFUPK8|4.0|This is a theatrical review of \\"Man of Steel\\" and may contain spoilers.<br /><br />Like Spider-Man and Batman, Superman gets a reboot as director Zack Snyder, with a big assist from producer Christopher Nolan, conjure a darker setting for the Krypton immigrant.  The film opens on the doomed planet Krypton where Jor-El (Russell Crowe) and Lara Lor-Van (Ayelet Zurer) have borne a child, conceived the old fashion way which is illegal based on  the government's genetically manipulative mandate.  Consistent with Superman lore, the planet will soon self-destruct mostly due poor management by the government.<br /><br />In actuality both Jor-El and Gen. Zod (Michael Shannon) have beefs with the government, but Zod acts on his own authority which gets him sentenced to a lifetime of floating in space.  Jor-El and Lara manage to send baby Kal-El into the void destined for Earth along with some magical codex which will allow Jor-El to materialize later and provide fatherly advice.  I was quite impressed with this original act.  The artwork is excellent and there is a nice mixture of advanced science mixed in with rides on flying dragon-like creatures.<br /><br />As the scene changes quickly to Clark Kent working on a fishing boat then a young Clark having to \\"save\\" a school bus that plunges into a lake, I'm wondering where all those earlier years went.  We do get to fill in the gaps as the film occasionally goes into flashback.  What makes this second act compelling is that we understand Clark/Kal-El's dilemma.  His adoptive parents, Jonathan and Martha Kent (nicely played by Kevin Costner and Diane Lane), believe Clark (a bulked up Henry Cavill) should keep his super powers a secret.  They are rightly concerned that this \\"difference\\" will ultimately be detrimental to his growth.  Mankind has a history of not always accepting others who may be different.<br /><br />Clark eventually leaves Kansas searching for the right answers.  This leads him to the Arctic where he finds his biological father in the form of a codex hologram.  Jor-El suggests that Clark was sent to Earth to improve human existence where they failed on Krypton.  Lois Lane (Amy Adams) has entered the picture by now.  She's a prize winning reporter who is searching for the mysterious man who has saved many lives.<br /><br />\\"Man of Steel\\" does depart from familiar legend in several ways.  First, Superman is only spoken once that I recall.  The \\"S\\" on the eventual suit is a Krypton symbol, not an \\"S.\\"  While Superman can indeed be weakened, it isn't by some glowing green rock.  Most interesting of all is that, there are few secrets between Clark and Lois.  We don't have to ask ourselves why Lois doesn't recognize that \\"Sup\\" is Clark with horned-rimmed glasses.<br /><br />So where does this movie begin to falter.  In the final act, as Superman must deal with Zod who was freed when Krypton exploded.  Zod, and his hot lieutenant and man hater Faora-Ul (Antje Traue), want the illegally conceived Kal-El destroyed and wants to take over Earth for his own species.  The movie goes into full out \\"Transformer\\"-styled destructive mode.  While some will feel this adrenaline rush is needed after the cerebral middle section, I found it tedious, loud and frankly, pretty boring.  We've all seen it before in \\"Thor,\\" \\"The Avengers\\" and many other movies.  It goes on forever. B00CEMH31Q|5.0|This is a really great Hanson album. I'm a little different than the typical Hanson fan. I'm in my late thirties and became a fan because of This Time Around, their second album. I was not a fan during Middle Of Nowhere/mmmbop.<br /><br />This album offers a little bit of everything. There's some rock with 'You Cant Stop Us' and Fired Up, some soul/motown sound with 'I've Got Soul,' 'Get the Girl Back,' and 'Tragic Symphony.'  The album also offers some straight pop and a couple ballads. Isaac also returns with lead vocals in 'For Your Love.' It also features their typical great harmony.<br /><br />1. Fired Up<br /><br />This song is a great rock song and a great way to start the album. I love the guitar in this song and it has great attitude. If you need to psyche yourself up for a game or a job interview this would be a great song to listen to.<br /><br />2. I've Got Soul<br />This song is a more soulful song. Good horns. Also features a guest vocal which is not typical of Hanson songs.<br /><br />3. You Can't Stop Us<br /><br />This is the second straight rock song of the album, featuring Zac and Taylor on lead. It is similar to Fired Up, but offers more powerful harmonies. It reminds me of 'Rest In Peace' by Extreme. Good guitar riffs.<br /><br />4. Get the Girl Back<br />This song is the most like the songs on Shout it Out and is the first single. The album version has a slightly more extended intro that I think adds a lot to the song. It features horns and harmony. It has the most Motown feel. I like the song, but it's not my favorite. There's actually too much cowbell, if that's possible. Catchy tune.<br /><br />5. Juliet<br />This is a Zac lead. I love this song. It's very sweet. It's a slower song but not a ballad. Some lines from 'Romeo and Juliet.' I really like the rhythm of this song. There are some strings in this song and it's piano driven. This is one of the gems of the album. The way he stutters when he says 'Juliet' is cute. I also think this is probably Zac's best vocal performance on an album.<br /><br />6. Already Home<br />The bridge makes this song. It has a huge sound that really makes this song. Great harmonies in this song. Guitar driven with some organ sound. They use a Hammond B3, a Wurlitzer, and a Rhodes piano on the album. I don't know enough to know which one is in this song, but it works well. Great beat and driving rhythm to this song. Maybe the most anthemic song on the record.<br /><br />7. For Your Love<br />This is Isaac's lead. It's a nice ballad. The slowest song of the album. It would make a great wedding song.<br /><br />8. Lost Without You<br />This is a power ballad. I don't like power ballads, but if you like power ballads then you will like this song. Good rhythm and harmonies. It's well done, I just don't like power ballads, so if it were the best power ballad on the planet Still wouldn't like it that much.<br /><br />9. Cut Right Through Me<br />This is a very catchy tune. Great harmony. Great combo of guitar and organ sound.<br /><br />10. Scream and Be Free<br />This is another Zac lead. This is a slower song but not a ballad. I really like it. Good lyrics. This will be a great song live.<br /><br />11. Tragic Symphony<br />This is my favorite song of the album. Great groove and attitude. Sounds more like Michael Jackson than any other song on the record. Also features a violin. I can't capture how good this song is by writing about it. You just have to listen to it.<br /><br />12. Tonight<br />This is a slower song and the longest on the record. It has a great sound, and more knowledgeable Hanson fans will love all of the hidden song references throughout the song. They reference many songs that appear on albums, starting with 'Rain' from Boomerang and even including songs from Fan Club cds. This features lead verses from Taylor and Isaac. Great harmonies in this song as well. A great song to end the album with.<br /><br />13. Save Me From Myself.<br />This is pretty much a bonus song for the Album. It's kind of depressing but still a good song. It features Zac on lead. It reminds me of 'Believe' from Underneath.<br /><br />This is a great album. I think it's their best work since This Time Around. The sound quality is also much better than Shout it Out for you audiophiles out there. There isn't a weak song on the record.

0062255657|4.0|Gaiman has offered up a simple story that speaks on childhood and memory. I've always enjoyed his particular perspective. He writes in a very personal, unafraid way. This is a short novel. It has its share of quirky thrills and exploration of myths and fables, but the real value of this book reveals itself in the voice of a tired, wounded adult remembering the way the world was when it seemed new. This book has been billed as a novel \\"for adults\\", but it feels aimed at the child within us all. With his usual blend of sweetness, melancholy and sometimes muted dread, Gaiman paints a world where all the barnacles life leaves us with become evident in comparison to what seemed most vital in our formative years. There is little of the complexity, action or intensity of some of his earlier works, but it would take a truly hard heart to eventually put this one down without a smile.<br /><br />Thanks, Neil. Innocence deserves its place still.

B0087X728K|5.0|Arctic Silver 5 is probably the best thermal compound that I have ever used, and I have used many. I have used it both in CPUs and GPUs and it does a phenomenal job at cooling my components. It keeps my 4770K very cool both in idle and under load. At idle the CPU stays around 33C and under load it hovers around 76C which is overclocked at 4.6Ghz. I'm using an H100i from Corsair to cool my CPU and it works very well with Artic Silver 5. The CPU stays below 65c while playing games such as Battlefield 3 and Crysis 3 on max settings.<br /><br />I know there are people out there who just go straight ahead and use the pre-applied thermal paste that comes with the CPU and get horrible temps. If you are going to spend a lot of money on a high end CPU then you might as well spend a few more bucks on a quality thermal compound. It doesn't add much to the cost of a build and it's worth it in the end because you will get much lower temps than with pre-applied thermal paste.<br /><br />Even when using Prime95, the CPU still stays very cool thanks to this awesome thermal paste. I use the pea method and have always gotten good results. I know some people use the single strip method right in the middle of the CPU and spread it out but I have found that the pea method works better.<br /><br />I did some comparisons against the pre-applied thermal paste that comes with most CPUs/GPUs and found out that Artic Silver 5 dropped my temps around 7-10c. Artic Silver 5 comes with plenty of paste that can last a long time. Make sure you do it right because some people have their own methods which sometimes works and sometimes doesn't. If you don't apply it right, you may even get worse temps than before. Putting just the right amount of thermal paste between your CPU and your cooler makes all the difference, trust me.<br /><br />My main rig:<br /><br />Case: Corsair 650D<br />GPU: EVGA GTX 780<br />CPU: Intel Core i7 4770K (still experimenting)<br />PSU: Corsair AX850<br />Ram: Kingston 16GB of RAM<br />SSD: Samsung 840 Pro 256GB<br />MB: ASUS Sabertooth Z87<br />OS: Windows 7 64bitof RAM<br />SSD: Samsung 840 Pro 256GB<br />MB: ASUS Sabertooth Z87<br />OS: Windows 7 64bit

Both Adams and Calvin play it very real and the movie is all the stronger for it. 0062255657|5.0|I, like many others, have been eagerly awaiting this book. It does not disappoint. Neil Gaiman has been known to write about the same thing in different (wonderful) ways. This is not a bad thing. What is it they say about a writer? That they are always writing the same book over and over, but in different exciting forms? I say this as a way to get in, as a preface to the fact that this book makes complete sense as part of his Work, and yet is irreparably different.<br /><br />In some ways, this novel is recognizably autobiographical - the author himself admits this in the afterword. It also happens to be his saddest novel. This novel may be only 192 pages, but it will seep into you. That is in fact, my only minor complaint - the shortness of the entire affair. Just when you get into the meat of the story, it's over. Yes, objectively, I can say - this is a tightly plotted novel - but I was never one to care much about plots. For me, it's all about the experience of getting to the end. I didn't want the characters to go away. I hope he revisits the Hampsteads at some point. They are just as worthy of a caveat as Shadow was in Fragile Things. Still, I don't think the shortness of the work detracts from it in any serious way. Certainly, it won't affect my rating.<br /><br />To reiterate - I read Gaiman for the liquidity and lushness of his prose, and his imagery, and the fascinating things he does with myth and metaphor. This book has all of that in spades. Just let it wash over you, like an ocean.*<br /><br />  *A little on the head, or nose, I know - but your body should be able to handle it.

However, the natural, competitive drive in him should have generated the effort.<br /><br />Granted, this Superman is no Romantic as was Richard Donner's,and this is all the more reason to invest in rich melody, dazzling counterpoint, and expansive orchestration. B000002J1Y|5.0|Wow!  A lot of words have been spilled over Yessongs here, so I won't add too many.  I'll just start by saying that Yessongs might be simply the greatest live album of all time, just so we're clear.<br /><br />Yessongs is one of those albums you can pull out again and again, year after year, and just get caught up in it all over again.  I remember when I was about 12 (1976) an acquaintance gave me his vinyl copy of Yessongs.  (He was going to college in northern California, smoking a lot of dope, and only listening to the Grateful Dead.)  I thought I had died and gone to heaven.  I played that thing so much I just about wore it out.  Now, nearly 40 years later, I find that I need to hear this album (on CD now) at least once every few months.<br /><br />So, what about this \\"progressive rock\\" thing?  Well, the fact is, Yes simply rocked harder than just about any other band.  Yes, their music is intricate -- some might even describe it as \\"symphonic\\" in the sense that it largely consists of tightly composed music that where every instrumental part must be reproduced faithfully in order to achieve the performance -- but that doesn't mean that it is bloodless or cold.  Quite the opposite!  And Yessongs, more than any other Yes album, demonstrates just how hard they could rock.<br /><br />If you have heard Yes's studio creations, then you might very well wonder how these 10- to 20-minute masterworks could possibly be reproduced live by five long-haired lads.  But, reproduce them they do!  Indeed, the live versions of these songs almost always outstrip the studio versions.  Particularly with the tracks from the Close to the Edge album (all of which are also on Yessongs), I would say that the live versions are all better.  For me, though, the high point of Yessongs is Yours is No Disgrace (from the Yes Album).  Steve Howe's extended solo here surely ranks as one of the all-time greatest guitar solos ever caught on tape.  The piece becomes a concerto for rock guitar.<br /><br />I will just finish by saying that Steve Howe is definitely the star here.  After hearing Yessongs (and watching the video), there is no mystery why Steve Howe won the Best Overall Guitarist category of the Guitar Player reader's poll five years in a row in the seventies.  No other rock guitarist at the time could even come close to his combination of technique, melodic inventiveness (he has been called \\"the Charlie Parker of rock guitar\\"), and versatility, and it is all on display in Yessongs.<br /><br />If you love music, and you haven't heard this album, then you know what to do...
